## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / dynamical concentration models)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of concentration A, which is the standard setup for chemical kinetics expressed as ordinary differential equations. With only (t, A) available, the most likely relationships are rate-law forms where dA_dt depends on A (reaction order, saturation/inhibition, autocatalysis) and possibly explicit time-dependence (time-varying rate constants, feeds, deactivation).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption/production: dA_dt = c0 (constant-rate formation or depletion, e.g., surface-limited or excess reactant)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (unimolecular growth/decay; sign of c0 sets production vs consumption)
- Pseudo-first-order with constant source/sink: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A (background generation plus first-order loss, or vice versa)
- Second-order / bimolecular (lumped): dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (effective second-order dependence when other reactant is proportional to A)
- General power-law (fractional order): dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (empirical/global rate law capturing complex mechanisms)
- Relaxation to equilibrium (linear driving force): dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A) (approach to steady state A = c1 under first-order exchange/relaxation)
- Autocatalytic / limited-capacity form: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (autocatalysis with depletion/limitation leading to sigmoidal A(t))
- Saturating (capacity-limited) rate in A: dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A) (rate increases with A then plateaus due to crowding/limited active sites)
- Substrate/product inhibition-like form: dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A**c2) (high-A suppression via inhibitory complexation/aggregation)
- Time-varying rate constant (linear drift): dA_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * A (rate constant changing over time due to ramping conditions)
- Time-varying rate constant (exponentially relaxing): dA_dt = (c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) * A (activation/deactivation or mixing transients affecting effective k(t))
- Forced/source-driven kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 * exp(c3 * t) (reaction term plus time-dependent feed/impulse-like input)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Reaction order identification: if dA_dt scales like A**n, log(|dA_dt|) vs log(A) is approximately linear with slope n (power-law rate laws).
- Equilibrium/steady-state approach: terms like (c1 - A) imply a stable fixed point at A = c1 and exponential relaxation when linearized.
- Autocatalysis signature: multiplicative A*(c1 - A) produces low initial rate (near A≈0), rapid mid-growth, then slowdown near A≈c1 (sigmoidal time course).
- Saturation with concentration: rational forms A/(1 + c*A) indicate diminishing returns at high A (site limitation, transport limitation, finite catalytic capacity).
- High-concentration inhibition: denominators with A**n (e.g., 1 + c*A**n) produce rate suppression at large A consistent with self-inhibition/product inhibition/aggregation.
- Time-dependent effective kinetics: k(t)*A structures suggest external condition changes (catalyst deactivation, changing illumination, mixing) rather than intrinsic mechanism changes in A alone.
- Constant source terms: additive +c0 indicates feed/production independent of A (inflow, baseline generation), shifting steady states and preventing full decay to zero.
- Sign constraints as mechanism clues: negative coefficient on A**n suggests consumption; positive suggests net formation; mixed signs (c0 + c1*A) often imply competing production and loss pathways.

Match coefficients by choosing:

  - \(c3=-0.6789593965981179\)
  - \(c5=0.1640697849676163\)
  - \(c4=0\)
Under domain \(A\ge 0\), this exactly equals GT. **Accept (conditional equivalence).**
